ARIE 1957-1958 [ARIE 076]

Annual Report on Indian Epigraphy for 1957-58. 19?? [Delhi]: [Manager of Publications (Department of Archaeology)].



[APPENDIX ]A.—COPPER PLATES, 1957-58



ANDHRA



ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/1 (page 12)
Place
Director of Archaeology, Andhra Pra-desh, Hyderabad. Through Dr. D.C.Sircar. Findspot: Amudalapadu, Alampur Taluk, Mahbubnagar Dis-trict.
Dynasty
Chālukya of Bādāmi
King
Vikramāditya I
Date
Year 5, Vaiśākha-paur-ṇamāsī.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Telugu-Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records the grant of the village of Iparuṁkal in the Vaṁgūravāḍi vishaya by the king when he was camping at the village of Marrūra, in favour of Sudarśanāchārya in payment of guru-dakshiṇā on the occasion of the king's Śiva-maṇḍala-dīkshā. Publi-shed in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXII, pp. 175 ff.; cf. Bhārati, May 1957, pp. 86 ff.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/2 (page 12)
Place
From Sri Manda Narasimham. Find-spot Arasavalli, Srikakulam District.
Dynasty
Eastern Gaṅga
King
Vajrahasta III
Date
Śaka 982, (kara-vasu-nidhi) Kārttika śu. 12, Monday = 1060. A.D., October 9.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit (prose & verse), Eastern Nāgarī.
Remarks
Issued from Kaliṅganagara. Registers the grant of the village Arisavalli situated in Varāhavartanī-vishaya, originally by the king to the son and three daughters of the mahā-pradhāna Dālama-peggaḍa. The lands in the village were divided into parts and were distributed among a number of persons. Published in Bhārati. May 1954, pp. 449 ff; J.A. H.R.S., Vol. XXI, pp. 113 ff.; Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXII, pp. 310 ff.


ASSAM



ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/3 (page 12)
Place
Department of Historical and Anti-quarian Studies, Gauhati.
Dynasty
Ahom
King
Gaurīnāthasiṁha
Date
Śaka 1714, Āshāḍha 23, Wednesday Irregular.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit & Assamese, Assamese
Remarks
Records the grant of land in favour of 83 dūtas or pāikas of Navagrāma.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/4 (page 12)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
(1) Śivasiṁha and Queen Ambikā. (2) Rājêśvarasiṁha.
Date
(1) Śaka 1654, Pausha 11 (2) Śaka 1682
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit & Assamese, Assamese
Remarks
Records the grant of some land together with 13 families of bhaṭakas and 2 families of pāikas as brahmōttara in favour of Bāṇêśvara Kêśavāchārya of Rāmadiya, by Śivasiṁha and his queen. It was renewed on the latter date by Rājêśvarasiṁha.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/5 (page 12)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Lakshmīsiṁha
Date
Śaka 1697, Phālguna
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit & Assamese, Assamese
Remarks
Records the grant of some land in favour of Kavisūrya and others who were the sons of Jayadêva Mêdhi. It is stated that some land at Manuhamāti-bila was previously granted by the Dihiṅgīya Baraphukana on behalf of the king in favour of the Brāhmaṇa Jayadêva who was the Mêdhi of the satra at Śilā-grāma in Bausi-pargana and that he was deprived of the land fraudulently by Kavichūḍāmaṇi. The present grant was made in compensation for the land lost.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/6 (page 12)
Place
Haiyungthal, Nowgong District
Dynasty
Sālastambha of Prā-gjyōtishapura.
King
Harjaravarman
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
Incomplete. Records the genealogy of the king and mentions the chief queen Maṅgalaśrī, the officials Yuvarāja Vanamāla, Mahāsainyapati Gaṇa, Mahādvārādhipati Jayadêva and others. In characters of about the 9th century A.D. Publi-shed in the Kāmarūpāśāsanāvali, pp. 44 ff. and Plate.


BENGAL, WEST



ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/7A-E (page 13)
Place
Superintendent, Archaeological section, Indian Museum, Calcutta.—Bronze images. Findspot:—Nagapattinam, Tanjore District, Madras.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Tamil
Remarks
Five labels which read as follows: (i) Ariyār-Nāyakar. (ii) Śaṅgāṇḍāḷ-Nāyakar. (iii) Āḷūḍai[ya*]piḷḷai. (iv) Aṇandar-dêvar. (v) Udayāṇḍāḷ ka (incomplete) Cf. The Nagapattinam and other Buddhist Bronzes, Bulletin of the Madras Government Museum, pp. 74, 82, 84 and 86. Plate XXIV, Nos. 18—22.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/8 (page 13)
Place
Do. Findspot:—Badakhimedi Estate, Ganjam.
Dynasty
Gaṅga of Śvētaka
King
Anantavarman
Date
Year 19, Phālguna su. 5
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Kaliṅga
Remarks
Records the grant of the village of Svalpa-Vêlura (or Svalpa-Vêlurō) in the Khalgukhaṇḍa vishaya by the king to Bhaṭṭa Nānaṭaśarman belonging to the Vatsa gōtra. The record was registered by the chief queen Śrīvāsa-bhaṭṭārikā while Mahāsāmanta Aśōkadêva acted as the dūtaka. The charter was composed by Mahāsāndhivigrahika Gōvinda-dêva, and engraved by Mahīndrabhīma. In characters of about the 7th and 8th centuries. A.D. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXIV, pp. 129 ff. and Plate.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/9 (page 13)
Place
Shri Kunja Govinda Goswami, Lecturer, Calcutta University. Findspot:—Gautami, Badakhimedi, Ganjam.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Indravarman
Date
Year 4, Phālguna, śu. 3.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Kaliṅga
Remarks
Records the gift of a piece of land in or near the village Salachaṇikā (or Salavaṇikā) of the Hêmvakama-ṭamva vishaya by the king to the Brāhmaṇas Vināya-kaśarman and another, both belonging to the Vāja-sanêya charaṇa, Parāśara gōtra and the Śakti-Kāṇva-Vaśishṭha pravara for the merit of his parents and himself. Do. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXIV, pp. 180 ff. and Plate.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/10 (page 13)
Place
Impressions from the Indian Museum, Calcutta. (Now deposited with the Sāhitya Parishad, Midnapore).
Dynasty
Gauḍa
King
Śaśāṅka
Date
Year 19, Bhādra 19
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, East Indian
Remarks
Records the gift of the village of Muhā-Kumbhāra-padraka to the meritorious priest Bhaṭṭêśvara of the Kāśyapa gōtra by Sāmanta Mahārāja Sōmadatta who is stated to be ruling over Utkala and Daṇḍa-bhukti. Published in J.A.S.B., Vol. XI, 1945, No. 1. pp. 1 ff.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/11 (page 13)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Do.
Date
Year 8, Pausha 12
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, East Indian
Remarks
Records the gift of land in the village of Kumbhāra-padraka in the Kê[ta]kapadrika to Dāmyasvāmin of the Bhāradvāja gōtra and Madhyandina śākhā by Mahāpratihāra Śubhakīrtti who was ruling over Daṇḍabhukti. Loc. cit.


BOMBAY



ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/12 (page 14)
Place
Impressions from Bhārata Itihāsa Saṁ-śōdhakamaṇḍala, Poona, Findspot: Devalali, Ahmednagar District.
Dynasty
Yādava of Dêvagiri
King
Bhillama III
Date
Śaka 974, Nandana, Pu-shya śu. 15, total eclipse of the moon, Tuesday = 1052 A.D., December 8.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Registers the king's grant of the four villages, viz., Kōṇamvā, Trayī, Pippalatthā and Māṅgala[ju]mara-hara, to a Brāhmaṇa called Śrīdhara-daṇḍanāyaka, whose great-grandfather Sillaṇa is said to have served Paramāra Vairisiṁha of Dhārā. The donee's family is stated to have hailed from Oyāri-grāma of the Madhya-dêsa. The grant was composed by the Kāyastha Taikataiya, son of Vijayaiya and was engraved by one Bhadra, son of Sōhanaiya. Contains another record in continuation of the above, regis-tering a grant of the village Dêulavalli in exchange for Kumarahara (?) by Sêüṇachandra (II).
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/13 (page 14)
Place
Do. Findspot: Mehunabare, East Khandesh District.
Dynasty
Sêndraka
King
Vairadêva stationed at Bahalāpurī
Date
Śaka 624, expired, Śrāvaṇa, ba. 11 Saṅkrānti, Vyatī-pāta = 702 A.D., July 24, Monday, f.d.t. ·46.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Registers the grant of the village called Dêvī-grama, situated at a distance of about two gavyūtas to the west of Bahalāpurī, by the chief who is described as the son of Daṇḍirāja and grandson of Dêvaśakti of the lineage of the Śêndraka kings to Nāgaśarman of the Kāśyapa gōtra and Vājasanêya śākhā, son of Nandisvāmin and grandson of Rêvasvāmin of Kāñchī-The writer of the charter was the Mahāsāndhivigrah-ādhikṛita Sāuaka.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/14 (page 14)
Place
Do. Findspot: Nandurbar, West Khan-desh.
Dynasty
Rāshṭrakūṭa
King
Gōvinda III
Date
Śaka 722 Pausha, Pūrṇimā, Monday, Uttarāyaṇa = 801 A.D., January 4.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Early Nāgarī
Remarks
Damaged. Records the gift of the village Kōṭṭāvara to fifty Brāhmaṇas of various gōtras by the king.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/15 (page 14)
Place
Tracing of seal. From St. Xavier's College. Bombay. Findspot: Bhitari Sayyidpur Tahsil, Ghazipur District, Uttar Pradesh.
Dynasty
Gupta
King
Kumāragupta II
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
A little less than the upper half of the seal is occupied by the emblem of Garuḍa with a snake coiled round his neck. The faint representations over the right and the left wings resemble the chakra or discus of Vishṇu and the śaṅkha or conchshell respectively. The inscription below, in relief, gives the genea-logy. Published in Ind. Ant., Vol. XIX, pp. 224 ff.

ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/17 (page 14)
Place
Deccan College Post-graduate and Research Institute, Poona. Through Dr. G.S.Gai.
Dynasty
Chālukya of Bādāmi
King
Vijayāditya
Date
Year 14, Śaka 632, Kārttika Paurṇimā.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records the grant of a village named Kāruve near Karahāṭanagara, on the bank of the Kṛishṇā (Veṇṇā) and a field at the latter city to Nāgulladêvaśarmman, by the king from his camp at Karahāṭanagara. The gift is stated to have been made at the request of Vikramāditya. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXVI, pp. 322 ff.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/18 (page 15)
Place
Do. Findspot: Khakurdi, Malegaon Taluk, Nasik District.
Dynasty
Rāshṭrakūṭa
King
Dantidurga
Date
Śaka 978 (Nāga-naga-aṅka), Kārttika, Darśa-tithi, So-lar eclipse. Probably = 1044 A.D., November 22, if the Śaka year is a mis-take for 966.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Early Nāgarī
Remarks
Mentions, besides the name of the king's father Amōgha-varsha, Karkkarāja who is said to have ruled from his capital at Mānakhêṭa. Records the gift of a land known as Khōggavāṭa in Mōharakhêṭaka to Gōvinda Bhaṭṭa of the Mādhyandina śākhā, son of Kōmmadêva and grandson of Daddapa of the Parā-śara gōtra. Published in BISM, Quarterly, Vol. XXI, No. 4.

ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/20 (page 15)
Place
Photographs of eye copies. Findspot: Kaira, Bombay. (Now deposited in the Library of the Royal Asiatic Society, London).
Dynasty
Gūrjara
King
Dadda II Praśāntarāga
Date
Kalachuri 380, Kārttika śu. 15.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Issued from Nāndīpura. Records the grant of the village of Śirīshapadraka in the Akrūrêśvara vishaya to forty Brāhmaṇas including Bhaṭṭi, the adhyāpaka, who came from Jambūsara and settled in the above village. The charter was written by Sandhivigrahādhi-karaṇādhikṛita Rêva. Published in JIAS, New Series, Vol. I, pp. 246. ff; Ind. Ant., Vol. XIII, pp. 81 ff.; CII, Vol. IV, pp. 57 ff.

Remarks

MADHYA PRADESH



ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/24 (page 15)
Place
Superintendent, Temple Survey Project, Northern Region, Bhopal. Through Dr. B.Ch.Chhabra.
Dynasty
Vākāṭaka
King
Pravarasêna II
Date
Year 29, Vaiśākha ba. 10 year 29, Vasê (Varshā) 5, diva. 2.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Box-headed
Remarks
Records the royal gift of the village Dhavavāsaka-Brāhmaṇa-vāṭaka to several Brāhmaṇas belonging to the Vāji-Kauṇḍinya sagōtra. The third plate of the record which contains the details about the donees is engraved indifferently and in a different hand.

Place
Do. Findspot: Kolavennu, Bezwada Taluk, Krishna District, Andhra.
Dynasty
Kākatīya
King
Gaṇapati
Date
Śaka 1172 (nayana-adri-rudra), Saumya, Māgha, solar eclipse. Irregular.
Language & Alphabet

ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/32 (page 16)
Place
Impressions and photographs from Sri Kannappa Naicker, Panchayat Board President, Alavay, Kalattūr, Chin-gleput District. Through Sri K.D. Swaminathan.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vêṅkaṭapati I
Date
Śaka 1524 (vêda-nêtra-kaḷ-amba-indu), Śubhakṛit, Māgha śu. 7 (Ratha-saptamī) = 1603 A.D., January 9.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nandi-Nāgarī
Remarks
Registers the grant of four villages, viz., Chittūru, Māmbāka, Agaram and Pūruvalupāka situated in Atsarvāka(Achcharapākka)-parru in Paḍaivīḍu-mahārājya by the king to Vāsudêva-bhaṭṭa, son of Raṅgapaiya, and grandson of Amaram Timmayya of the Ātrêya gōtra, Āśvalāyana sūtrā and Ṛik śākhā. The four villages were constituted into one unit and renamed as Dattātrêyapuram. The charter was composed by one Chidambarakavi, the nephew of Śivasūrya, and was engraved by Kāmayāchārya, son of Gaṇapaya and the younger brother of Vīraṇa.
ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/33 (page 17)
Place
Pārijātavanêśvara temple, Tirukkalar, Tanjore District.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Rājādhirāja I
Date
Year 31
Language & Alphabet
Tamil
Remarks
Registers an arrangement made by a certain Tirumaṇap-pichchaṇ, who bore the surname Ariaiyan Nāgarai-yaṇ and Mahīpālakulakāla-ppêraraiyan, whereby another Brāhmaṇa was appointed to perform worship in addition to the one who was already doing it in the temple at Tirukkaḷar. In characters of the 11th century. Published in SII, Vol. III, Pt. IV, pp. 469-70.


MYSORE



ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/34 (page 17)
Place
From Sri N.Tatachar, Chintamani. Through Sri B.R.Gopal.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vīra Harihara
Date
Śaka 1153, Āṅgirasa, Chai-tra śu. 10, Monday. Irregular.
Language & Alphabet
Telugu
Remarks
Records a gift of income from taxes to Śrīnivāsa Rāmaliṅga Purāṇikulayya by the Ten Thousand dêvāṅgas (weavers), in the presence of god Rāmaya-dêva and goddess Chauḍêśvarī, on the occasion when, in the presence of the king, it was decided that the dêvāṅgas were entitled for Paṁchavaṁne biruda and Yajñōpavīta (sacred thread). In late characters.


ORISSA



ARIE/1957-1958/A/1957-58/35 (page 17)
Place
From Sri Panchanan Sandi of Ratnagiri, Jaipur, Cuttack. Through Sri Sadashiv Rath Sarma and Super-intendent, Department of Archaeo-logy, Eastern Circle, Calcutta.
Dynasty
Sōmakula of Trika-liṅga.
King
Karṇadêva alias Mahāśiva-gupta.
Date
Year 6, Āśvina śu. 12
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Issued from Yayātinagara. Records the grant of the village of Kōṇā in Brahme-Aṭṭahāvīsa-khaṇḍa by the king to Rāṇī Karppūraśrī who hailed from the mahāvihāra at Salōṇapura in Utkala-dêśa. Records that in the specified year the king of Burma and his chief queen visited Bōdh-Gayā, worshipped the Bōdhi tree and offered numerous jewels including 511 diamonds, 311 Haritamaṇi, 3966 rubies and 623 muktā and also built a chaitya there. Cf. List of Inscriptions in Burma, Vol. I, pp. 280 ff., Nos. 1228 and 1229.

Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records a grant of an oil mill for burning a perpetual lamp to God Svayaṁbhu Śivaliṅgadêva. The donor of the grant was Mākaladêvi, the wife of Mahāmaṇḍa-lêśvara Sahadêva-daṇḍanāyaka.
ARIE/1957-1958/B/1957-58/211 (page 39)
Place
Fifth pillar in the same place
Dynasty
Do.
King
Kannara
Date
Śaka 11[8]0, Kāḷayukta, Mārgaśira Pūrṇimā, Tuesday, lunar eclipse. Probably = 1258 A.D., November 12. The month was, however, Nija-Kārttika accord-ing to the Indian Ephe-meris.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
States that when Mahadêva-rāṇeya was governing the divisions of Tardavāḍi and Kaṇambaḍe, a subordinate of his (name not clear) made a grant of an oil mill to God Svayaṁbhu Śivaliṅgadêva. The gift was entrust-ed into the hands of [Śrīmūrti] Śivadêva, the āchārya of the temple. Mahājanas of Vijayāpura are referred to.

Chāḷukya Vikrama year 39, Jaya, Pushya ba. Ekā-daśī, Thursday, Uttarā-yaṇa-saṁkramaṇa = 1114 A.D., December 24. The saṁkramaṇa occurred on the next day.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records the Kaḷaśārōhaṇa of a temple (name lost) by Chandrabhūshaṇa-paṁḍita when Daṇḍanāyaka Gōvindarasa, a subordinate of Mahāpradhāna Bāṇasaverggaḍe Anantapāḷa was governing Nāgara-khaṇḍa-70. Further records some gifts (details lost) to Kāḷa of the Āṅgirasa-Bārhaspatya-Bhāradvāja gōtra by Sākimayya, son of Hattiya Vāmanayya, and others.
ARIE/1957-1958/B/1957-58/311 (page 48)
Place
Slab set up by the side of Hariharê-Īśvara temple.
Dynasty
Hoysaḷa
King
Vīra-Ballāḷa II
Date
Śaka 1126, Rudhirōdgārin, Phālguna śu. 3, Thurs-day = 1204 A.D., Febru-ary 5. The Śaka year was current.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records the construction of the temple of Hariharêśvara by Veṁṇala-seṭṭikavve, wife of Kāmi-seṭṭi, an elaborate account of whose genealogy is given, and registers gifts of land, garden, oil-mill and income from several taxes to the deity by the king camping at Haḷḷavura, at the instance of Sarvvādhikāri Kaṁma-ṭada Mallayya who was governing Sattaḷige-70 and Nāgarakhaṇḍa-70. The gifts were made over to Āchārya Haraśaktidêva.

Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records the installation of Chandrêśvaraliṅga by Chandra, the mahāprabhu of Taḷakavāvi, situated in Keḷavāḍi, a subdivision of Eḍedore-nāḍu. ARIE/1957-1958/B/1957-58/379 (page 55)
Place

Dynasty
Yādava
King
Siṅghaṇa

Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Enumerates the conquests of Siṅghaṇa. Gives an eulogistic account of Mahāmaṇḍalêśvara Immaḍi Mallidêvarasa of the Ahihêya family and of Bêchi-seṭṭi and Rêchi-seṭṭi, the seṭṭiguttas of Moraṭa-300. Records the installation of a liṅga by the two seṭṭis in the name of their father. States that they also made a grant of land and money to Śaṅkara-paṇḍita for the purpose of worshipping the god Tryambakesvara.

V.S. 887, Vaiśākha ba. 2.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Damaged. Seems to record the consecration of the image of god Nīlalōhita by the guru Gāmuṇḍasvāmin. The name of the composer is given as Kṛishṇa, son of Bhaṭṭa Gōvinda. The idol was made by tapasa in Jajjasvāmin and the inscription was engraved by Dêddaṭa, son of Atigaṇādita. Noticed in A.R. Rajputana Mus., Ajmer. 1920-21, p. 2.

Remarks
Fragmentary. Records the construction of a temple for the god Vindhyêśvaradêva by Uddalladêvī, dau-ghter of Mahāsāmanta Bharahadêva of the Rāshṭra (Rāshṭrakūṭa) family of Kānyakubjadêśa and chief queen of Mahamandadêva who was a subordinate of the king. FOREIGN COUNTRIES



PAKISTAN, WEST



PUNJAB



ARIE/1957-1958/B/1957-58/321 (page 81)
Place
Government Museum, Lahore.—Find-spot: Pehoa, Karnal District.
Dynasty
Gūrjara Pratihāra
King
Mahêndrapāla
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the building of a triple temple of Vishṇu by Gōgga, Pūrṇarāja and Dêvarāja belonging to the Tōmara family and assigning three villages, Yaksha-pālaka, Gejjara and Pāṭala for the bhōga of the deity. Achyuta, son of Rāma, was the architect. The com-poser of the praśasti whose name is lost was the son of Bhaṭṭa Rāma and the engraver was [.] ālāditya, son of Durlabhāditya. In characters of the 9th or 10th century A.D. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. I, pp. 242 ff. and Plate.
